  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_bea12f84-9d79-4c34-9906-196235a921c9'
      });

  <span id="freeText13407810986171691023" style="display:none">If a big hungry moose comes to visit, you might give him a muffin to make him feel at home. If you give him a muffin, he'll want some jam to go with it. When he's eaten all your muffins, he'll want to go to the store to get some more muffin mix. <p> In this hilarious sequel to <i> If You Give a Mouse a Cookie,</i> the young host is again run ragged by a surprise guest. Young readers will delight in the comic complications that follow when a little boy entertains a gregarious moose. </p><p> Children's Choices for 1992 (IRA/CBC)</p></span>

  <span id="freeText12349464845719393487" style="display:none">If you give someone an inch, they'll take a mile. <i>If You Give a Moose a Muffin</i>, he'll overrun your whole house. It's an interesting take on the dangers of desires, and how easy it is to never be satisfied. As the moose gets his way, the things he wants are more and more far-fetched and make for a super fun adventure.<br /><br />The story is the sequel to the much better known <i>If You Give a Mouse a Cookie</i>. It seems like in the second version Numeroff did everything better: it's less repetitive and the illustrations are way more fun.</span>

  <span id="freeText14411775179655562637" style="display:none">I tell you what, you will have a busy day if you give a moose a muffin. They have lots of ideas of what they want. It becomes important to be able to say NO to a Moose or they will eat all your muffins. I thought this book was very cute. I love the Moose in a sweater, wonderful. <br /><br />The artwork is fun and full of mischief. The moose has some personality and there is always a mess following him. Backgrounds are mostly blank white and I don't care for that as much. I think I would say this is sort of one of those comedy of errors. <br /><br />A great silly beginning book. I love it. </span>

<div id="review_1127276113" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1127276113" />
    <a title="Leah Jackman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34667800-leah-jackman"><img alt="Leah Jackman" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1127276113?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leah Jackman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leah Jackman" href="/user/show/34667800-leah-jackman">Leah Jackman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34667800-leah-jackman?shelf=picture-books">picture-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1127276113" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6038045593604679413">In this hilarious sequel to If You Give a Mouse a Cookie, the young host is again run ragged by a surprise guest. Young readers will delight in the comic complications that follow when a little boy entertains a gregarious moose. Laura Joffe Numeroff does an amazing job at giving us all the perspectives and using amazing language and imagery. The illustrations really bring the story to life. This story always makes me smile and laugh. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_993987639" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/993987639" />
    <a title="A." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32403186-a"><img alt="A." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422744705p2/32403186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/993987639?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="A." class="user" itemprop="url" name="A." href="/user/show/32403186-a">A.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32403186-a?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32403186-a?shelf=childrens-books">childrens-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32403186-a?shelf=humor">humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer993987639" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer248129340704821202">(The following review has been written for comedy purposes for my cousin's birthday. It may get weird. Read at your own risk.)<br/><br/>*Happy Birthday, Sara!*<br/>I'll say this again, if anyone gives /this/ book anything lower than three stars, they had a rough childhood of much repression and they probably need to see a counselor. Or maybe they realized how god-awfully greedy this freaking moose is. Spoilers are below, though why that's necessary to see for a book where the title literally gives away the plo</span>
  <span id="freeText248129340704821202" style="display:none">(The following review has been written for comedy purposes for my cousin's birthday. It may get weird. Read at your own risk.)<br /><br />*Happy Birthday, Sara!*<br />I'll say this again, if anyone gives /this/ book anything lower than three stars, they had a rough childhood of much repression and they probably need to see a counselor. Or maybe they realized how god-awfully greedy this freaking moose is. Spoilers are below, though why that's necessary to see for a book where the title literally gives away the plot line and is therefore a spoiler in itself, I haven't a clue. Alright, let's get this train on the tracks, despite the tracks being very long and with very many twists and turns that'll take your heart on a whirlwind of emotions. Or not, this isn't The Fault In Our Stars or anything. If it was, the title might be "If You Give a Moose A Cigarette" and would go on to say that he'll promptly refuse your lighter and blather on about metaphors or whatever. Anyway! <br />Laura Joffe (like the middle name, not the douchey GoT character) Numeroff writes this book about one rather large moose with a questionable past and very severe MADD, which here stands for "Moose Attention Deficit Disorder." The very title page includes said moose munching on a few garden leaves, thus foreshadowing the mischief he's sure to get into in the following pages. <br />Right away we have a child sticking his body out of the window of his lovely stone house to offer a curious moose a bit of baked goods. Clearly, this kid never learned not to talk to strangers. The muffin is procured by the moose and suddenly the little asshole thinks that was an open invitation to barge right in through the doors. Has this thing ever learned manners? This is the Black Bear story all over again! Oh, great, now he wants jam too. Where do you get off asking for a place to chill AND jam after being offered one tiny muffin?<br />Oh yes, give him the jam your mother slaved over for hours last night while she sobbed about how her husband left her alone with child, that's nice. Of course, after he finishes more of the muffins that your bereaving mother cooked up, he'll wipe his muddy hooves on the tablecloth and want more! And he STILL wants more! This moose is far too greedy. Then he turns the little boy into his bitch by making him go out and get him some more mix. Like the kid's old enough to use the oven! Fast forward a bit.<br />This story is basically just a way for the moose to ruin ALL of the kid's mothers things. The sweater, the socks, the living room floor, and the bedsheets! And this child has no concern for who has to clean it all up, because he certainly won't have to. This poor mother just wants to drink herself happy and enjoy her garden, but she can't even have that! I bet the moose will drink all of the liquor in her cabinet by next sequel. <br />Then the stupid moose goes outside RIGHT BEHIND WHERE THE MOTHER IS and you remember that she's been home all along so I guess that makes her half a decent parent. But then you take it back because a moose walks over to her clothsline, puts a sheet onto it with magically little trouble, and walks back into the house to play with her son and she has no idea. The bitch is so drunk off her ass that she didn't even notice a very LARGE moose in her yard. I started out saying this book is 5 star worthy, only now I'm not so sure. She follows them into the house and they make a break for it before she could see them. "Oh my kid's just playing with a giant moose, how nice. I must've overdone it on the drugs." <br />There's literally no lesson learned here. Big Black Bear teaches a lesson on manners and includes a turning point. This book is a circle. A CIRCLE. After all their antics are over, the moose is tired and hungry and suddenly wants nothing more than a muffin again. Jesus Christ, man! Where's the lesson? This teaches children to be privileged little brats who can just do whatever they want if their mom doesn't see it. I smell 'Rugrats' type of story here. Anyway, Happy Birthday, Sara. Enjoy your day like I enjoyed ripping this book to shreds in the non-literal sense. You're an awesome cousin and you'll pass all your classes next semester, so chill out a bit, will ya? And give Elvis some treats. It's not his fault your getting old. </span>
  <a data-text-id="248129340704821202" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_136062356" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/136062356" />
    <a title="Brian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4690092-brian"><img alt="Brian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310496780p2/4690092.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/136062356?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brian" href="/user/show/4690092-brian">Brian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4690092-brian?shelf=wishlist">wishlist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4690092-brian?shelf=revisit">revisit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4690092-brian?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4690092-brian?shelf=in-full">in-full</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer136062356" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1923689262497468315">I love children's book authors. Not constrained by demands for realism, they are presented with opportunities to venture into interesting creative spaces, and a few of them produce true gems as a result. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/826584.If_You_Give_a_Moose_a_Muffin__If_You_Give____' title='If You Give a Moose a Muffin (If You Give...) by Laura Joffe Numeroff' rel='nofollow noopener'>If You Give a Moose a Muffin</a> is a perfect example. The concept is simple and a tad ridiculous. Moose (plural) love muffins. But there is inherent danger in feeding a wild animal: if you give a moose a muffin, he'll want some jam to go with it. Once you handed over the jam, though, he has a new d</span>
  <span id="freeText1923689262497468315" style="display:none">I love children's book authors. Not constrained by demands for realism, they are presented with opportunities to venture into interesting creative spaces, and a few of them produce true gems as a result. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/826584.If_You_Give_a_Moose_a_Muffin__If_You_Give____" title="If You Give a Moose a Muffin (If You Give...) by Laura Joffe Numeroff" rel="nofollow noopener">If You Give a Moose a Muffin</a> is a perfect example. The concept is simple and a tad ridiculous. Moose (plural) love muffins. But there is inherent danger in feeding a wild animal: if you give a moose a muffin, he'll want some jam to go with it. Once you handed over the jam, though, he has a new demand, and so on, and so on, <i>ad infinitum</i>.<br /><br />These stories are a child's introduction to the absurd, and they're great fun. The illustrations are fabulous, whimsical, and colorful. They really bring out the characters of the moose and little boy, and have wonderful little touches and details hidden throughout.<br /><br />I always enjoyed this book when I was very young, and I'm sure I could enjoy it just as much today. It's a top notch "learn to read" piece, and one that I will definitely be sharing with my children one day.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1923689262497468315" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159157425" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3887345075837541135">When I first read this book when I was younger I did not see the thrill in this book. There was no plot, no climax, and a poor setting but after I used this book for a supported reading project I grew to understand the importance of this book. For my supported reading project I used this book for the cause and effect aspect and after the students heard the read aloud they wrote down their favorite cause and effect moment on a notecard. Prior to the lesson I had made many different cause and effe</span>
  <span id="freeText3887345075837541135" style="display:none">When I first read this book when I was younger I did not see the thrill in this book. There was no plot, no climax, and a poor setting but after I used this book for a supported reading project I grew to understand the importance of this book. For my supported reading project I used this book for the cause and effect aspect and after the students heard the read aloud they wrote down their favorite cause and effect moment on a notecard. Prior to the lesson I had made many different cause and effect notecards and the students played a simple game like memory with the cards. The students really enjoyed the game and I got a whole new respect for Laura Numeroff books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3887345075837541135" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_98926141" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98926141" />
    <a title="Josiah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1914201-josiah"><img alt="Josiah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1239682454p2/1914201.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98926141?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Josiah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Josiah" href="/user/show/1914201-josiah">Josiah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98926141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12836736288038264868">Essentially identical in style to <i>If You Give a Mouse a Cookie</i>, this companion volume written by Laura Joffe Numeroff has the same basic points of charm to it that the previous book had. It's funny to see how such an "ordinary" action as offering a muffin to a hungry moose can trip so many little effects that cause the moose to bounce from one activity to the next, never quite finishing any of them, until at last the moose's forays lead him all the way back around to the beginning again, asking </span>
  <span id="freeText12836736288038264868" style="display:none">Essentially identical in style to <i>If You Give a Mouse a Cookie</i>, this companion volume written by Laura Joffe Numeroff has the same basic points of charm to it that the previous book had. It's funny to see how such an "ordinary" action as offering a muffin to a hungry moose can trip so many little effects that cause the moose to bounce from one activity to the next, never quite finishing any of them, until at last the moose's forays lead him all the way back around to the beginning again, asking for a muffin and some blackberry jam.<br /><br /> <i>If You Give a Moose a Muffin</i> functions well as an early reader, providing a smooth story that's not too long to keep the attention of its target age group.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12836736288038264868" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1228281635" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1228281635" />
    <a title="Mark Baker" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4545420-mark-baker"><img alt="Mark Baker" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389574977p2/4545420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1228281635?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark Baker" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark Baker" href="/user/show/4545420-mark-baker">Mark Baker</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4545420-mark-baker?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4545420-mark-baker?shelf=picture-book">picture-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1228281635" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6426334825662075764">When you spot a moose outside your window, you might be tempted to offer it a muffin. But what is a muffin without jam? And what might the moose want to do next?<br/><br/>As with all the charming books from this pair, the story is wild and yet plenty of fun. As the connections are made, they actually do make sense even if the end results is wild. There is plenty of humor along the way both from those connections and the wonderful illustrations.<br/><br/>Read my full review at <a href='http://carstairsconsiders.blogspot.com/2015/03/book-review-if-you-give-moose-muffin-by.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Carstairs Considers</a>.</span>
  <span id="freeText6426334825662075764" style="display:none">When you spot a moose outside your window, you might be tempted to offer it a muffin. But what is a muffin without jam? And what might the moose want to do next?<br /><br />As with all the charming books from this pair, the story is wild and yet plenty of fun. As the connections are made, they actually do make sense even if the end results is wild. There is plenty of humor along the way both from those connections and the wonderful illustrations.<br /><br />Read my full review at <a href="http://carstairsconsiders.blogspot.com/2015/03/book-review-if-you-give-moose-muffin-by.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Carstairs Considers</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6426334825662075764" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9897843793110780161">The book “If You Give A Moose A Muffin” by Laura Numeroff is classified as juvenile fiction; targeting ages 3 to 7. This book is a good selection for teaching about chain reaction and/or cause-and-effect; also its a humorous sequel in the “If You Give… picture book series. The story has vocabulary enrichment for emergent readers; the illustrations are colorful and simple; the story is lighthearted and fun.</span>

<div id="review_3022001708" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3022001708" />
    <a title="Shikara Walker" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/104426247-shikara-walker"><img alt="Shikara Walker" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3022001708?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shikara Walker" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shikara Walker" href="/user/show/104426247-shikara-walker">Shikara Walker</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104426247-shikara-walker?shelf=week-2">week-2</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3022001708" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14451217222069240535">Definitely an all time favorite of mine! I prefer this version over the others (we have copies of this, Pig/Pancake and Mouse/Cookie at the house) and I read it with my four year old often. This book reminds me of the ways life can twist and turn with every decision we make and how new options are formed with every choice. Text-to-Teaching Connection: the class is to make their own book where each page is written by a different student based off the flow of previous pages. The good thing about t</span>
  <span id="freeText14451217222069240535" style="display:none">Definitely an all time favorite of mine! I prefer this version over the others (we have copies of this, Pig/Pancake and Mouse/Cookie at the house) and I read it with my four year old often. This book reminds me of the ways life can twist and turn with every decision we make and how new options are formed with every choice. Text-to-Teaching Connection: the class is to make their own book where each page is written by a different student based off the flow of previous pages. The good thing about this is that the style of this writing can be used as an ELA activity incorporating any subject(s) and grade level. After the book is written, the teacher can read the book out loud so the students can see how different the book turned out once it left their hands. Makes for a wonderful group activity too.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14451217222069240535" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3577461333" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3577461333" />
    <a title="Kira Cook" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/122347638-kira-cook"><img alt="Kira Cook" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3577461333?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kira Cook" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kira Cook" href="/user/show/122347638-kira-cook">Kira Cook</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3577461333" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6085273052774218499">This book follows similar story structure as the other animal books in this series. It is great for beginning readers. The easy vocabulary and familiar content will allow for independent reading for beginning readers after some adult readings. The pictures go along with the story well and will allow kids to understand the story better if they are reading on their own. I would recommend this book to younger readers. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YnTcoq0Q+f28Dlcv1AQiXzKvf3cLvaKD8fnfVCcm0YDi8msMcmY6HsBhMV5/dfuFhbD46YEgUuysud6PMns1kg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('E9bcNkmUvQC1XKoCd5FP1PFcUAkpkJAcUAVaPlvjRUGTUGuYluJ+48kzzHPc4JYORkPXl6MNYHMNRVvlTr6hUw==')})
  }
//]]>

<span id="freeTextContainer10300970497925623881">Laura Joffe Numeroff is the <i>NYT</i> best-selling author of <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/767680.If_You_Give_a_Mouse_a_Cookie' rel='nofollow noopener'>If You Give a Mouse a Cookie</a>, </i><i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/776391.What_Mommies_Do_Best_What_Daddies_Do_Best' rel='nofollow noopener'>What Mommies/Daddies Do Best</a>
</i> and <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/51843079-raising-a-hero' rel='nofollow noopener'>Raising a Hero</a>.</i> She was born in Brooklyn, New York and graduated from Pratt Institute. Laura grew up as the youngest of three girls, surrounded by art, music, and books. An avid animal lover, Laura has always wanted to write a book about service dogs. She now lives in Los Angel</span>
  <span id="freeText10300970497925623881" style="display:none">Laura Joffe Numeroff is the <i>NYT</i> best-selling author of <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/767680.If_You_Give_a_Mouse_a_Cookie" rel="nofollow noopener">If You Give a Mouse a Cookie</a>, </i><i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/776391.What_Mommies_Do_Best_What_Daddies_Do_Best" rel="nofollow noopener">What Mommies/Daddies Do Best</a>
</i> and <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/51843079-raising-a-hero" rel="nofollow noopener">Raising a Hero</a>.</i> She was born in Brooklyn, New York and graduated from Pratt Institute. Laura grew up as the youngest of three girls, surrounded by art, music, and books. An avid animal lover, Laura has always wanted to write a book about service dogs. She now lives in Los Angeles, California.</span>

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
